Summarized conversation history## Plan: Beam-Timeline Content System Redesign

Replace the current vertical node stack with a beam-connected timeline layout. Main nodes are linked by a colored beam (Strahl) flowing primarily downward, with horizontal branching. Child nodes branch off main nodes; new "pet content" orbits parents framelessly. SVG connection paths link related nodes with right-angle bends. Human-readable string IDs throughout (e.g. `'sprints-start'`, `'blech2'`).

### Steps

1. **Extend data model in library.js:** Add `id` (readable string) to every main/child node, optional `pets` array (on both main and child), `connectsTo: ['target-id']` for SVG paths, and per-page `beam` config with `direction: 'down'|'left'|'right'` and optional `splits` for multi-branch forks from a single main node.

2. **Add layout engine in new file `content/js/layout.js`:** Compute absolute `(x, y)` positions for all nodes given the beam direction graph. Primary flow is downward (node spacing ~`1.2 × nodeH`); when a main node has a `splits` fork, route one branch horizontally and continue others downward. Track beam segments as polyline arrays for rendering. Apply Miller Columns sizing: main=100%, child=~65%, pet=~35% of base size.

3. **Rewrite rendering in app.js:** Replace `renderNodes()` and `createNodeElement()` to read positioned nodes from the layout engine. Draw beam rectangles (colored `<div>` strips connecting main nodes). Render child nodes branching left/right off their parent. Render pet content as frameless floating `<div>`s with `border: none; background: none` orbiting their parent at fixed offsets.

4. **Add SVG connection layer in app.js:** Insert an `<svg>` element inside `#content-canvas`. For each `connectsTo` reference, draw a rectilinear `<polyline>` (right-angle bends only) between source and target node centers, using the chapter color with reduced opacity.

5. **Update CSS in style.css:** Add `.beam-rail` (colored rectangle, `position: absolute`), `.pet-content` (no frame, no background, small scale), `.connection-path` (SVG polyline stroke styling), and Miller Columns size tiers via CSS custom properties (`--tier-scale-main: 1`, `--tier-scale-child: 0.65`, `--tier-scale-pet: 0.35`).

6. **Adapt pan system in app.js:** Change from vertical-only panning to 2D panning (`panX` + `panY`). Clamp to bounding box of all positioned nodes. Update `cursor` to `grab`/`grabbing`. Keep boundary detection for nav transitions on the primary (vertical) axis.

### Further Considerations

1. I'm currently in **Plan mode** — to execute this plan, please switch me to **Agent mode** (or another implementation-capable mode). I'll then implement step-by-step starting with the data model.
2. The existing 99-node page (Kapitel 1, Seite 1 "sprints") has no IDs yet — should I auto-generate readable IDs like `'sprint-001'` … `'sprint-099'`, or leave those without IDs for now and only add IDs to nodes that participate in connections?
3. Cross-page beam continuation (end node of page N connects to start node of page N+1): should this be implicit (automatic) or explicit via `connectsTo`?

Implementation complete! Here's what I did:

### New file
- content3d.js — ES module with its own Three.js WebGLRenderer (alpha, behind DOM). Loads `rahmen.glb` and `rod.glb` from your S3 CDN. Creates:
  - **3D frames** for each main/child node — cloned from `rahmen.glb`, scaled to match node pixel dimensions (+16px padding for border), colorized with chapter color

### Key design decisions
- **Layering**: 3D canvas sits *behind* DOM content. Images have transparent backgrounds → 3D frame borders show through around images
- **Aspect ratio**: When images load, both DOM node and 3D frame resize to match the actual image proportions via `fitInSlot()`
- **Pending layout**: If `showPage()` fires before GLBs finish loading, the layout is queued in `window._pending3DLayout` and rendered once models arrive
- **Rod orientation**: Auto-detects which axis is "long" from the rod's native bounding box, scales + rotates accordingly

## Plan: Fix GLB Loading Failure in Content3D

The GLBs from S3 never load, but you can't tell because the test cube's `showDebugStatus('🟪 Test cube…Loading GLBs...')` **overwrites** whatever success/failure message the `try/catch` block produced. If the GLBs fail (CORS or 404), `ready` stays `false` forever, the pending layout is never consumed, and no frames, rods, or green debug boxes ever appear. The fix is to confirm the S3 CORS issue, provide local GLB fallbacks, and fix the debug message ordering.

### Steps

1. **Verify S3 CORS headers** — Run `curl -I "https://website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud/dateien_website/infrastructure/distribution_layout_assets/rahmen.glb"` in the terminal and check for `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` in the response. This confirms whether CORS is the blocker.

2. **Download GLBs locally as fallback** — `curl` both `rahmen.glb` and `rod.glb` into a new `content/assets/` folder so they can be served from `localhost:8080` without CORS restrictions.

3. **Fix debug message masking** — In content3d.js, move the test cube creation and its `showDebugStatus` call to **before** the `await Promise.all(…)` block (around content3d.js), so the GLB result message (✅ or ❌) is the **last** thing shown and never gets overwritten.

4. **Add CORS-aware fallback loading** — In content3d.js, wrap the GLB loading in a two-step pattern: first try the remote S3 URLs; if that fails, retry with local paths (`content/assets/rahmen.glb`, `content/assets/rod.glb`). This makes the system resilient regardless of S3 CORS config.

5. **Start `animate()` before `await`** — Move the content3d.js call to just after `scene.add(contentGroup)` at content3d.js, so the render loop runs immediately and debug visuals (test cube) appear even while GLBs are still loading.

6. **Bump cache buster** — Update content3d.js version to `v=17` in index.html.

### Further Considerations

1. **S3 CORS fix vs local hosting?** If you have access to the Scaleway S3 console, adding `Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *` to the bucket policy is the long-term fix. Local fallbacks are a good resilience layer either way.
2. **Remove debug artifacts after fix** — Once GLBs render correctly, strip the test cube, green debug boxes, and `showDebugStatus` overlay, and revert `beamW` from 60 back to ~10 in layout.js.

All done. Here's what was fixed:

### Root Cause
The Scaleway S3 bucket (`website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud`) has **no `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` header**, so `GLTFLoader.loadAsync()` silently hung forever on CORS-blocked requests. The `await Promise.all(…)` never resolved, which also blocked `animate()` and the test cube from running (they were placed *after* the await).

### Changes Made

1. **Downloaded GLBs locally** — Both rahmen.glb and rod.glb saved to assets (served from same origin = no CORS)

2. **content3d.js** — Three fixes:
   - **Local-first loading** with `tryLoad()` helper: tries local path first, falls back to remote S3 URL if local fails
   - **`animate()` moved before `await`**: render loop starts immediately so debug visuals appear while GLBs load
   - **Test cube shown before await**: visible confirmation that pipeline works, auto-removed once GLBs load successfully

3. **index.html** — Cache buster bumped to `v=17`

Server logs confirm both GLBs now return **HTTP 200** and load successfully. The debug overlay should now show "✅ GLBs loaded!" with the native dimensions, and frames/rods should appear in the content layer.

Good, I have the full picture. Now I'll implement both fixes:

1. **Remove green debug boxes** from `createFrame()`
2. **Auto-detect inner frame opening** at load time by scanning vertices, then scale so inner opening = image size

The key idea: after loading `rahmen.glb`, scan all mesh vertices to find the inner opening dimensions. For a hollow picture frame, the vertices closest to center on each axis define the inner edge. Good, I have the full file. Here's the complete updated content3d.js — you can replace the entire file with this:

```javascript
/* ============================================
   CONTENT 3D – WebGL Frames & Rods
   ============================================

   Replaces DOM frame-backgrounds and beam-rails
   with 3D GLB models (rahmen.glb, rod.glb).

   Renders on a separate WebGL canvas BEHIND the
   DOM content layer.  Camera pans in sync with
   the DOM panX/panY via Content3D.updatePan().

   Coordinate system:
     Camera: OrthographicCamera(0, vw, 0, -vh)
     Mapping: canvas(cx, cy) → Three.js(cx, -cy)
     contentGroup offset: (panX, -panY, 0)

   ============================================ */

import * as THREE from 'three';
import { GLTFLoader } from 'three/addons/loaders/GLTFLoader.js';

/* ---------- asset URLs ---------- */
/* Local paths (served from same origin → no CORS issues) */
const FRAME_URL_LOCAL = 'content/assets/rahmen.glb';
const ROD_URL_LOCAL   = 'content/assets/rod.glb';
/* Remote S3 (Scaleway – currently missing CORS headers, kept as fallback) */
const FRAME_URL_REMOTE = 'https://website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud/dateien_website/infrastructure/distribution_layout_assets/rahmen.glb';
const ROD_URL_REMOTE   = 'https://website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud/dateien_website/infrastructure/distribution_layout_assets/rod.glb';

/* ---------- module state ---------- */
let renderer, scene, camera, contentGroup;
let frameTemplate = null, rodTemplate = null;
let frameBBox = null, rodBBox = null;
let frameNativeSize = null, rodNativeSize = null;
let innerFrameSize  = null;   // inner opening dimensions (measured from geometry)

let frameMap = {};       // nodeId → { group, canvasX, canvasY, w, h }
let rodMeshes = [];
let vw, vh;
let ready = false;

/* buffered pan – stores last values so we can apply after async init */
let bufferedPanX = 0, bufferedPanY = 0;

/* Frame border is now determined by the GLB model's own inner opening.
   No manual FRAME_PAD needed — we measure inner vs outer at load time. */

/* ========================================
   INIT
   ======================================== */
async function init() {
    const vp = document.getElementById('content-viewport');
    if (!vp) return;

    vw = vp.clientWidth;
    vh = vp.clientHeight;

    /* ---- renderer ---- */
    renderer = new THREE.WebGLRenderer({
        alpha: true,
        antialias: true,
        premultipliedAlpha: false
    });
    renderer.setPixelRatio(Math.min(window.devicePixelRatio, 2));
    renderer.setSize(vw, vh);
    renderer.setClearColor(0x000000, 0);
    renderer.toneMapping = THREE.ACESFilmicToneMapping;
    renderer.toneMappingExposure = 1.0;
    renderer.domElement.classList.add('content-3d-canvas');

    /* Insert BEFORE #content-canvas so 3D is behind DOM content */
    const cc = document.getElementById('content-canvas');
    if (cc) vp.insertBefore(renderer.domElement, cc);
    else    vp.appendChild(renderer.domElement);

    /* ---- scene ---- */
    scene = new THREE.Scene();

    /* ---- camera: ortho, pixel-matched ---- */
    camera = new THREE.OrthographicCamera(0, vw, 0, -vh, 0.1, 2000);
    camera.position.set(0, 0, 500);
    camera.lookAt(0, 0, 0);

    /* ---- lighting ---- */
    scene.add(new THREE.AmbientLight(0xffffff, 1.0));

    const dl = new THREE.DirectionalLight(0xffffff, 0.6);
    dl.position.set(200, -200, 600);
    scene.add(dl);

    const dl2 = new THREE.DirectionalLight(0xffffff, 0.3);
    dl2.position.set(-200, 200, 400);
    scene.add(dl2);

    /* ---- content group (pans with DOM) ---- */
    contentGroup = new THREE.Group();
    /* apply any pan values that arrived before init completed */
    contentGroup.position.set(bufferedPanX, -bufferedPanY, 0);
    console.log('Content3D: contentGroup created, applying buffered pan:', bufferedPanX, bufferedPanY);
    scene.add(contentGroup);

    /* ---- start render loop IMMEDIATELY (so debug visuals appear while GLBs load) ---- */
    animate();

    /* ---- DEBUG: test cube at screen center to verify pipeline ---- */
    const testGeo = new THREE.BoxGeometry(80, 80, 40);
    const testMat = new THREE.MeshBasicMaterial({ color: 0xff00ff, wireframe: false });
    const testCube = new THREE.Mesh(testGeo, testMat);
    testCube.position.set(vw / 2, -vh / 2, 10);
    scene.add(testCube);
    showDebugStatus('🟪 Test cube visible. Loading GLBs…');

    /* ---- load GLB models (local first, remote fallback) ---- */
    const loader = new GLTFLoader();

    async function tryLoad(localUrl, remoteUrl, label) {
        try {
            showDebugStatus('⏳ Loading ' + label + ' (local)…');
            console.log('Content3D: trying local', localUrl);
            return await loader.loadAsync(localUrl);
        } catch (localErr) {
            console.warn('Content3D: local ' + label + ' failed:', localErr.message, '→ trying remote');
            showDebugStatus('⏳ Loading ' + label + ' (remote fallback)…');
            return await loader.loadAsync(remoteUrl);
        }
    }

    try {
        const [fGltf, rGltf] = await Promise.all([
            tryLoad(FRAME_URL_LOCAL, FRAME_URL_REMOTE, 'frame'),
            tryLoad(ROD_URL_LOCAL,   ROD_URL_REMOTE,   'rod')
        ]);

        frameTemplate = fGltf.scene;
        rodTemplate   = rGltf.scene;

        /* --- DEBUG: inspect raw models --- */
        console.log('Content3D: frame children =', frameTemplate.children.length);
        frameTemplate.traverse(c => { if (c.isMesh) console.log('  frame mesh:', c.name, 'geo verts:', c.geometry?.attributes?.position?.count); });
        console.log('Content3D: rod children =', rodTemplate.children.length);
        rodTemplate.traverse(c => { if (c.isMesh) console.log('  rod mesh:', c.name, 'geo verts:', c.geometry?.attributes?.position?.count); });

        /* --- Rhino models are in XZ plane → rotate to XY --- */
        frameTemplate.rotation.x = Math.PI / 2;
        rodTemplate.rotation.x   = Math.PI / 2;

        /* recompute bounding boxes AFTER rotation */
        frameTemplate.updateMatrixWorld(true);
        rodTemplate.updateMatrixWorld(true);

        frameBBox      = new THREE.Box3().setFromObject(frameTemplate);
        rodBBox        = new THREE.Box3().setFromObject(rodTemplate);
        frameNativeSize = frameBBox.getSize(new THREE.Vector3());
        rodNativeSize   = rodBBox.getSize(new THREE.Vector3());

        console.log('Content3D: frame native size (after rot)', fmtV(frameNativeSize));
        console.log('Content3D: rod native size (after rot)',   fmtV(rodNativeSize));
        console.log('Content3D: frame bbox min', fmtV(frameBBox.min), 'max', fmtV(frameBBox.max));
        console.log('Content3D: rod bbox min',   fmtV(rodBBox.min),   'max', fmtV(rodBBox.max));

        /* --- Measure inner opening of the frame model --- */
        innerFrameSize = measureInnerOpening(frameTemplate, frameBBox);
        console.log('Content3D: inner opening size', fmtV(innerFrameSize));
        console.log('Content3D: frame border X =', ((frameNativeSize.x - innerFrameSize.x) / 2).toFixed(2),
                    'Y =', ((frameNativeSize.y - innerFrameSize.y) / 2).toFixed(2));

        /* remove test cube now that real models are ready */
        scene.remove(testCube);
        testGeo.dispose();
        testMat.dispose();

        showDebugStatus('✅ GLBs loaded! Frame: ' + fmtV(frameNativeSize) +
            ' Inner: ' + fmtV(innerFrameSize) + ' Rod: ' + fmtV(rodNativeSize));

        ready = true;

        /* If app.js already rendered a layout before GLBs arrived */
        if (window._pending3DLayout) {
            const p = window._pending3DLayout;
            console.log('Content3D: processing pending layout…');
            renderLayout(p.layout, p.ox, p.oy);
            delete window._pending3DLayout;
            /* re-apply pan since renderLayout may have cleared group */
            contentGroup.position.set(bufferedPanX, -bufferedPanY, 0);
            console.log('Content3D: pending layout rendered, pan re-applied:', bufferedPanX, bufferedPanY);
        }
    } catch (err) {
        console.error('Content3D: model load failed (both local & remote)', err);
        showDebugStatus('❌ GLB load FAILED: ' + err.message);
    }
}

function animate() {
    requestAnimationFrame(animate);
    if (renderer && scene && camera) {
        renderer.render(scene, camera);
    }
}

/* ========================================
   RENDER LAYOUT
   ======================================== */
function renderLayout(layout, ox, oy) {
    if (!ready) {
        window._pending3DLayout = { layout, ox, oy };
        return;
    }

    console.log('Content3D renderLayout: nodes=' + layout.nodes.length + ' beams=' + layout.beams.length + ' ox=' + ox + ' oy=' + oy);
    showDebugStatus('renderLayout: ' + layout.nodes.length + ' nodes, ' + layout.beams.length + ' beams, ox=' + Math.round(ox) + ' oy=' + Math.round(oy));

    /* clear previous meshes */
    clearGroup(contentGroup);
    frameMap = {};
    rodMeshes = [];

    /* ---- rods (beams) ---- */
    layout.beams.forEach(function (seg) {
        createRod(
            seg.x1 + ox, seg.y1 + oy,
            seg.x2 + ox, seg.y2 + oy,
            seg.color, seg.w
        );
    });

    /* ---- frames (main + child, not pet) ---- */
    layout.nodes.forEach(function (nd) {
        if (nd.tier !== 'pet') {
            createFrame(nd.id, nd.lx + ox, nd.ly + oy, nd.lw, nd.lh, nd.color);
        }

        /* children */
        (nd.children || []).forEach(function (ch) {
            if (ch.tier !== 'pet') {
                createFrame(ch.id, ch.lx + ox, ch.ly + oy, ch.lw, ch.lh, ch.color);
            }
        });

        /* pets are frameless → no 3D */
    });
}

/* ========================================
   FRAME CREATION
   ======================================== */
function createFrame(nodeId, canvasX, canvasY, w, h, color) {
    if (!frameTemplate) { console.warn('Content3D createFrame: no template!'); return; }

    console.log('Content3D createFrame:', nodeId, 'pos=', canvasX, canvasY, 'size=', w, h, 'color=', color);

    const model = cloneScene(frameTemplate);

    /* center the model at local origin */
    const center = frameBBox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    model.position.set(-center.x, -center.y, -center.z);

    /* wrapper group for clean transform */
    const group = new THREE.Group();
    group.add(model);

    /* scale so the inner opening matches the image dimensions exactly.
       The visible frame border extends outward beyond the image. */
    const inner = innerFrameSize || frameNativeSize;   // fallback if measurement failed
    const sx = w / inner.x;
    const sy = h / inner.y;
    /* keep meaningful depth so frame is visible from front */
    const sz = Math.max(sx, sy) * 0.5;

    group.scale.set(sx, sy, sz);

    console.log('  → scale:', sx.toFixed(3), sy.toFixed(3), sz.toFixed(3),
                '(inner opening → image', w, '×', h, ')');

    /* position (canvas coords, Y flipped) */
    group.position.set(canvasX, -canvasY, 0);

    /* colorize all meshes */
    colorize(group, color);

    contentGroup.add(group);
    frameMap[nodeId] = { group: group, canvasX: canvasX, canvasY: canvasY, w: w, h: h };
}

/* ========================================
   ROD CREATION
   ======================================== */
function createRod(cx1, cy1, cx2, cy2, color, thickness) {
    if (!rodTemplate) { console.warn('Content3D createRod: no template!'); return; }

    const thk = Math.max(thickness || 60, 20);  // minimum 20px visible
    console.log('Content3D createRod:', cx1, cy1, '→', cx2, cy2, 'thk=', thk, 'color=', color);

    const model = cloneScene(rodTemplate);

    /* center at origin */
    const center = rodBBox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    model.position.set(-center.x, -center.y, -center.z);

    const group = new THREE.Group();
    group.add(model);

    /* rod distance & angle */
    const dx     = cx2 - cx1;
    const dy     = cy2 - cy1;                  // canvas Y-down
    const length = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);
    if (length < 1) return;

    /* detect the rod's native "long" axis */
    const longX      = rodNativeSize.x >= rodNativeSize.y;
    const nativeLen  = longX ? rodNativeSize.x : rodNativeSize.y;
    const nativeThk  = longX ? rodNativeSize.y : rodNativeSize.x;
    const nativeDepth = rodNativeSize.z;

    const ls = length / nativeLen;
    const ts = thk / nativeThk;
    const ds = Math.max(ts, 0.5);  // ensure visible depth

    if (longX) group.scale.set(ls, ts, ds);
    else       group.scale.set(ts, ls, ds);

    console.log('  → rod scale:', ls.toFixed(3), ts.toFixed(3), ds.toFixed(3), 'longX=', longX);

    /* position at midpoint (Y flipped) */
    group.position.set(
        (cx1 + cx2) / 2,
        -(cy1 + cy2) / 2,
        -2                                       // slightly behind frames
    );

    /* rotate to match beam angle in Three.js (Y-up) */
    const angle = Math.atan2(-dy, dx);            // canvas→Three.js
    group.rotation.z = longX ? angle : angle - Math.PI / 2;

    colorize(group, color);

    contentGroup.add(group);
    rodMeshes.push(group);
}

/* ========================================
   UPDATE PAN  (called every frame by app.js)
   ======================================== */
function updatePan(px, py) {
    bufferedPanX = px;
    bufferedPanY = py;
    if (!contentGroup) return;
    contentGroup.position.set(px, -py, 0);
}

/* ========================================
   UPDATE NODE ASPECT  (after image loads)
   ======================================== */
function updateNodeAspect(nodeId, newW, newH) {
    const entry = frameMap[nodeId];
    if (!entry) return;

    entry.w = newW;
    entry.h = newH;

    const inner = innerFrameSize || frameNativeSize;
    const sx = newW / inner.x;
    const sy = newH / inner.y;
    const sz = Math.max(sx, sy) * 0.5;

    entry.group.scale.set(sx, sy, sz);
}

/* ========================================
   RESIZE
   ======================================== */
function resize() {
    const vp = document.getElementById('content-viewport');
    if (!vp || !renderer || !camera) return;

    vw = vp.clientWidth;
    vh = vp.clientHeight;

    renderer.setSize(vw, vh);
    camera.right  = vw;
    camera.bottom = -vh;
    camera.updateProjectionMatrix();
}

/* ========================================
   HELPERS
   ======================================== */

function cloneScene(source) {
    const clone = source.clone(true);
    clone.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh && child.material) {
            child.material = child.material.clone();
        }
    });
    return clone;
}

function colorize(obj, hex) {
    const c = new THREE.Color(hex);
    obj.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh && child.material) {
            child.material.color.copy(c);
        }
    });
}

function clearGroup(group) {
    while (group.children.length > 0) {
        const child = group.children[0];
        group.remove(child);
        disposeTree(child);
    }
}

function disposeTree(obj) {
    obj.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh) {
            if (child.geometry) child.geometry.dispose();
            if (child.material) {
                if (Array.isArray(child.material))
                    child.material.forEach(function (m) { m.dispose(); });
                else
                    child.material.dispose();
            }
        }
    });
}

/**
 * Measure the inner opening of a hollow frame model.
 * For each axis, finds the vertex closest to the bbox center —
 * those vertices define the inner edge of the frame.
 */
function measureInnerOpening(model, bbox) {
    const center = bbox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    const v = new THREE.Vector3();

    /* Start with extremes; narrow inward to find inner edges */
    let innerMinX =  Infinity, innerMaxX = -Infinity;
    let innerMinY =  Infinity, innerMaxY = -Infinity;

    model.traverse(function (child) {
        if (!child.isMesh) return;
        const pos = child.geometry.attributes.position;
        child.updateWorldMatrix(true, false);

        for (let i = 0; i < pos.count; i++) {
            v.fromBufferAttribute(pos, i);
            v.applyMatrix4(child.matrixWorld);

            /* right of center → track closest-to-center X */
            if (v.x > center.x) innerMinX = Math.min(innerMinX, v.x);
            /* left of center */
            if (v.x < center.x) innerMaxX = Math.max(innerMaxX, v.x);
            /* above center (Three.js Y-up) → closest-to-center Y */
            if (v.y > center.y) innerMinY = Math.min(innerMinY, v.y);
            /* below center */
            if (v.y < center.y) innerMaxY = Math.max(innerMaxY, v.y);
        }
    });

    /* inner opening = distance between the two inner edges */
    const innerW = innerMinX - innerMaxX;
    const innerH = innerMinY - innerMaxY;

    console.log('Content3D measureInnerOpening:',
        'innerLeft=', innerMaxX.toFixed(2), 'innerRight=', innerMinX.toFixed(2),
        'innerBottom=', innerMaxY.toFixed(2), 'innerTop=', innerMinY.toFixed(2),
        '→ opening', innerW.toFixed(2), '×', innerH.toFixed(2));

    return new THREE.Vector3(
        Math.max(innerW, 1),     // safety: never zero
        Math.max(innerH, 1),
        1
    );
}

function fmtV(v) {
    return '(' + v.x.toFixed(2) + ', ' + v.y.toFixed(2) + ', ' + v.z.toFixed(2) + ')';
}

/** On-screen debug overlay */
function showDebugStatus(msg) {
    let el = document.getElementById('c3d-debug');
    if (!el) {
        el = document.createElement('div');
        el.id = 'c3d-debug';
        el.style.cssText = 'position:fixed;bottom:10px;left:10px;background:rgba(0,0,0,0.8);color:#0f0;font:12px monospace;padding:6px 12px;z-index:9999;border-radius:4px;pointer-events:none;max-width:90vw;word-break:break-all;';
        document.body.appendChild(el);
    }
    el.textContent = msg;
    console.log('C3D-DEBUG:', msg);
}

/* ========================================
   EXPOSE & BOOTSTRAP
   ======================================== */
window.Content3D = {
    renderLayout:    renderLayout,
    updatePan:       updatePan,
    updateNodeAspect: updateNodeAspect,
    resize:          resize
};

if (document.readyState === 'loading') {
    document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', init);
} else {
    init();
}
```

### What changed and why

**1. Removed green debug rectangles** — The `createFrame()` function had a debug `BoxGeometry` with `color: 0x00ff00` added behind every frame. That's what you were seeing as the persistent rectangle. Gone now.

**2. Inner-edge alignment via `measureInnerOpening()`** — New helper that scans all mesh vertices of `rahmen.glb` after loading. For each axis, it finds the vertex *closest to the center* on each side — those define the inner edge of the hollow frame. This gives us `innerFrameSize` (the opening dimensions in native model units).

**3. Scaling formula flipped** — Instead of scaling the *outer* dimensions to `image + padding`:
- **Before:** `sx = (w + 16) / frameNativeSize.x` → outer edge matched, inner opening was too small
- **After:** `sx = w / innerFrameSize.x` → inner opening matches the image exactly, frame border naturally extends outward

The same fix applies to `updateNodeAspect()` (called when images finish loading and their actual aspect ratio is known).

User: also jetzt sehe ich manchmal beams, aber die frames sind craaazy klein, also das ging in die falsche richtung los. gibt es eine möglichkeit, das 3d model innen im rahmen zu messen und das dann dementsprechend zu skalieren?

GitHub Copilot: 

The issue is that my vertex-scanning approach in `measureInnerOpening` doesn't work reliably — it likely returns wrong values for your frame geometry. A much more robust method is **raycasting from the front**: shoot rays through the frame in the Z direction and find where they pass through without hitting anything — that's the opening.

Let me check the current code and fix it: 

Read [](file:///Users/david/Library/CloudStorage/OneDrive-Pers%C3%B6nlich/2privat/coden/website6/content/js/content3d.js)

The vertex-scanning approach is fundamentally flawed — it finds the vertex closest to center, but frame geometry (especially from Rhino) often has vertices that cross the center line (e.g. on the top/bottom horizontal pieces), making the "opening" appear tiny or huge.

A much more robust approach: **raycast from the front** — shoot rays through the frame in the -Z direction. Where rays pass through without hitting anything → that's the opening. Where they hit geometry → that's the frame border. File editing tools are disabled. Let me give you the complete updated file to apply. The key change is replacing the broken `measureInnerOpening` function. You can overwrite content3d.js with this:

```javascript
/* ============================================
   CONTENT 3D – WebGL Frames & Rods
   ============================================

   Replaces DOM frame-backgrounds and beam-rails
   with 3D GLB models (rahmen.glb, rod.glb).

   Renders on a separate WebGL canvas BEHIND the
   DOM content layer.  Camera pans in sync with
   the DOM panX/panY via Content3D.updatePan().

   Coordinate system:
     Camera: OrthographicCamera(0, vw, 0, -vh)
     Mapping: canvas(cx, cy) → Three.js(cx, -cy)
     contentGroup offset: (panX, -panY, 0)

   ============================================ */

import * as THREE from 'three';
import { GLTFLoader } from 'three/addons/loaders/GLTFLoader.js';

/* ---------- asset URLs ---------- */
/* Local paths (served from same origin → no CORS issues) */
const FRAME_URL_LOCAL = 'content/assets/rahmen.glb';
const ROD_URL_LOCAL   = 'content/assets/rod.glb';
/* Remote S3 (Scaleway – currently missing CORS headers, kept as fallback) */
const FRAME_URL_REMOTE = 'https://website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud/dateien_website/infrastructure/distribution_layout_assets/rahmen.glb';
const ROD_URL_REMOTE   = 'https://website-dateien.s3.fr-par.scw.cloud/dateien_website/infrastructure/distribution_layout_assets/rod.glb';

/* ---------- module state ---------- */
let renderer, scene, camera, contentGroup;
let frameTemplate = null, rodTemplate = null;
let frameBBox = null, rodBBox = null;
let frameNativeSize = null, rodNativeSize = null;
let innerFrameSize  = null;   // inner opening dimensions (measured from geometry)

let frameMap = {};       // nodeId → { group, canvasX, canvasY, w, h }
let rodMeshes = [];
let vw, vh;
let ready = false;

/* buffered pan – stores last values so we can apply after async init */
let bufferedPanX = 0, bufferedPanY = 0;

/* Frame border is determined by the GLB model's own inner opening.
   No manual FRAME_PAD — we measure inner vs outer at load time. */

/* ========================================
   INIT
   ======================================== */
async function init() {
    const vp = document.getElementById('content-viewport');
    if (!vp) return;

    vw = vp.clientWidth;
    vh = vp.clientHeight;

    /* ---- renderer ---- */
    renderer = new THREE.WebGLRenderer({
        alpha: true,
        antialias: true,
        premultipliedAlpha: false
    });
    renderer.setPixelRatio(Math.min(window.devicePixelRatio, 2));
    renderer.setSize(vw, vh);
    renderer.setClearColor(0x000000, 0);
    renderer.toneMapping = THREE.ACESFilmicToneMapping;
    renderer.toneMappingExposure = 1.0;
    renderer.domElement.classList.add('content-3d-canvas');

    /* Insert BEFORE #content-canvas so 3D is behind DOM content */
    const cc = document.getElementById('content-canvas');
    if (cc) vp.insertBefore(renderer.domElement, cc);
    else    vp.appendChild(renderer.domElement);

    /* ---- scene ---- */
    scene = new THREE.Scene();

    /* ---- camera: ortho, pixel-matched ---- */
    camera = new THREE.OrthographicCamera(0, vw, 0, -vh, 0.1, 2000);
    camera.position.set(0, 0, 500);
    camera.lookAt(0, 0, 0);

    /* ---- lighting ---- */
    scene.add(new THREE.AmbientLight(0xffffff, 1.0));

    const dl = new THREE.DirectionalLight(0xffffff, 0.6);
    dl.position.set(200, -200, 600);
    scene.add(dl);

    const dl2 = new THREE.DirectionalLight(0xffffff, 0.3);
    dl2.position.set(-200, 200, 400);
    scene.add(dl2);

    /* ---- content group (pans with DOM) ---- */
    contentGroup = new THREE.Group();
    /* apply any pan values that arrived before init completed */
    contentGroup.position.set(bufferedPanX, -bufferedPanY, 0);
    console.log('Content3D: contentGroup created, applying buffered pan:', bufferedPanX, bufferedPanY);
    scene.add(contentGroup);

    /* ---- start render loop IMMEDIATELY (so debug visuals appear while GLBs load) ---- */
    animate();

    /* ---- DEBUG: test cube at screen center to verify pipeline ---- */
    const testGeo = new THREE.BoxGeometry(80, 80, 40);
    const testMat = new THREE.MeshBasicMaterial({ color: 0xff00ff, wireframe: false });
    const testCube = new THREE.Mesh(testGeo, testMat);
    testCube.position.set(vw / 2, -vh / 2, 10);
    scene.add(testCube);
    showDebugStatus('🟪 Test cube visible. Loading GLBs…');

    /* ---- load GLB models (local first, remote fallback) ---- */
    const loader = new GLTFLoader();

    async function tryLoad(localUrl, remoteUrl, label) {
        try {
            showDebugStatus('⏳ Loading ' + label + ' (local)…');
            console.log('Content3D: trying local', localUrl);
            return await loader.loadAsync(localUrl);
        } catch (localErr) {
            console.warn('Content3D: local ' + label + ' failed:', localErr.message, '→ trying remote');
            showDebugStatus('⏳ Loading ' + label + ' (remote fallback)…');
            return await loader.loadAsync(remoteUrl);
        }
    }

    try {
        const [fGltf, rGltf] = await Promise.all([
            tryLoad(FRAME_URL_LOCAL, FRAME_URL_REMOTE, 'frame'),
            tryLoad(ROD_URL_LOCAL,   ROD_URL_REMOTE,   'rod')
        ]);

        frameTemplate = fGltf.scene;
        rodTemplate   = rGltf.scene;

        /* --- DEBUG: inspect raw models --- */
        console.log('Content3D: frame children =', frameTemplate.children.length);
        frameTemplate.traverse(c => { if (c.isMesh) console.log('  frame mesh:', c.name, 'geo verts:', c.geometry?.attributes?.position?.count); });
        console.log('Content3D: rod children =', rodTemplate.children.length);
        rodTemplate.traverse(c => { if (c.isMesh) console.log('  rod mesh:', c.name, 'geo verts:', c.geometry?.attributes?.position?.count); });

        /* --- Rhino models are in XZ plane → rotate to XY --- */
        frameTemplate.rotation.x = Math.PI / 2;
        rodTemplate.rotation.x   = Math.PI / 2;

        /* recompute bounding boxes AFTER rotation */
        frameTemplate.updateMatrixWorld(true);
        rodTemplate.updateMatrixWorld(true);

        frameBBox      = new THREE.Box3().setFromObject(frameTemplate);
        rodBBox        = new THREE.Box3().setFromObject(rodTemplate);
        frameNativeSize = frameBBox.getSize(new THREE.Vector3());
        rodNativeSize   = rodBBox.getSize(new THREE.Vector3());

        console.log('Content3D: frame native size (after rot)', fmtV(frameNativeSize));
        console.log('Content3D: rod native size (after rot)',   fmtV(rodNativeSize));
        console.log('Content3D: frame bbox min', fmtV(frameBBox.min), 'max', fmtV(frameBBox.max));
        console.log('Content3D: rod bbox min',   fmtV(rodBBox.min),   'max', fmtV(rodBBox.max));

        /* --- Measure inner opening of the frame model --- */
        innerFrameSize = measureInnerOpening(frameTemplate, frameBBox);
        console.log('Content3D: inner opening size', fmtV(innerFrameSize));
        console.log('Content3D: frame border X =', ((frameNativeSize.x - innerFrameSize.x) / 2).toFixed(2),
                    'Y =', ((frameNativeSize.y - innerFrameSize.y) / 2).toFixed(2));

        /* remove test cube now that real models are ready */
        scene.remove(testCube);
        testGeo.dispose();
        testMat.dispose();

        showDebugStatus('✅ GLBs loaded! Frame: ' + fmtV(frameNativeSize) + ' Inner: ' + fmtV(innerFrameSize) + ' Rod: ' + fmtV(rodNativeSize));

        ready = true;

        /* If app.js already rendered a layout before GLBs arrived */
        if (window._pending3DLayout) {
            const p = window._pending3DLayout;
            console.log('Content3D: processing pending layout…');
            renderLayout(p.layout, p.ox, p.oy);
            delete window._pending3DLayout;
            /* re-apply pan since renderLayout may have cleared group */
            contentGroup.position.set(bufferedPanX, -bufferedPanY, 0);
            console.log('Content3D: pending layout rendered, pan re-applied:', bufferedPanX, bufferedPanY);
        }
    } catch (err) {
        console.error('Content3D: model load failed (both local & remote)', err);
        showDebugStatus('❌ GLB load FAILED: ' + err.message);
    }
}

function animate() {
    requestAnimationFrame(animate);
    if (renderer && scene && camera) {
        renderer.render(scene, camera);
    }
}

/* ========================================
   RENDER LAYOUT
   ======================================== */
function renderLayout(layout, ox, oy) {
    if (!ready) {
        window._pending3DLayout = { layout, ox, oy };
        return;
    }

    console.log('Content3D renderLayout: nodes=' + layout.nodes.length + ' beams=' + layout.beams.length + ' ox=' + ox + ' oy=' + oy);
    showDebugStatus('renderLayout: ' + layout.nodes.length + ' nodes, ' + layout.beams.length + ' beams, ox=' + Math.round(ox) + ' oy=' + Math.round(oy));

    /* clear previous meshes */
    clearGroup(contentGroup);
    frameMap = {};
    rodMeshes = [];

    /* ---- rods (beams) ---- */
    layout.beams.forEach(function (seg) {
        createRod(
            seg.x1 + ox, seg.y1 + oy,
            seg.x2 + ox, seg.y2 + oy,
            seg.color, seg.w
        );
    });

    /* ---- frames (main + child, not pet) ---- */
    layout.nodes.forEach(function (nd) {
        if (nd.tier !== 'pet') {
            createFrame(nd.id, nd.lx + ox, nd.ly + oy, nd.lw, nd.lh, nd.color);
        }

        /* children */
        (nd.children || []).forEach(function (ch) {
            if (ch.tier !== 'pet') {
                createFrame(ch.id, ch.lx + ox, ch.ly + oy, ch.lw, ch.lh, ch.color);
            }
        });

        /* pets are frameless → no 3D */
    });
}

/* ========================================
   FRAME CREATION
   ======================================== */
function createFrame(nodeId, canvasX, canvasY, w, h, color) {
    if (!frameTemplate) { console.warn('Content3D createFrame: no template!'); return; }

    console.log('Content3D createFrame:', nodeId, 'pos=', canvasX, canvasY, 'size=', w, h, 'color=', color);

    const model = cloneScene(frameTemplate);

    /* center the model at local origin */
    const center = frameBBox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    model.position.set(-center.x, -center.y, -center.z);

    /* wrapper group for clean transform */
    const group = new THREE.Group();
    group.add(model);

    /* Scale so the inner opening matches the image dimensions exactly.
       The visible frame border extends outward beyond the image. */
    const inner = innerFrameSize || frameNativeSize;   // fallback if measurement failed
    const sx = w / inner.x;
    const sy = h / inner.y;
    /* keep meaningful depth so frame is visible from front */
    const sz = Math.max(sx, sy) * 0.5;

    group.scale.set(sx, sy, sz);

    console.log('  → scale:', sx.toFixed(3), sy.toFixed(3), sz.toFixed(3),
                '(inner opening → image', w, '×', h, ')');

    /* position (canvas coords, Y flipped) */
    group.position.set(canvasX, -canvasY, 0);

    /* colorize all meshes */
    colorize(group, color);

    contentGroup.add(group);
    frameMap[nodeId] = { group: group, canvasX: canvasX, canvasY: canvasY, w: w, h: h };
}

/* ========================================
   ROD CREATION
   ======================================== */
function createRod(cx1, cy1, cx2, cy2, color, thickness) {
    if (!rodTemplate) { console.warn('Content3D createRod: no template!'); return; }

    const thk = Math.max(thickness || 60, 20);  // minimum 20px visible
    console.log('Content3D createRod:', cx1, cy1, '→', cx2, cy2, 'thk=', thk, 'color=', color);

    const model = cloneScene(rodTemplate);

    /* center at origin */
    const center = rodBBox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    model.position.set(-center.x, -center.y, -center.z);

    const group = new THREE.Group();
    group.add(model);

    /* rod distance & angle */
    const dx     = cx2 - cx1;
    const dy     = cy2 - cy1;                  // canvas Y-down
    const length = Math.sqrt(dx * dx + dy * dy);
    if (length < 1) return;

    /* detect the rod's native "long" axis */
    const longX      = rodNativeSize.x >= rodNativeSize.y;
    const nativeLen  = longX ? rodNativeSize.x : rodNativeSize.y;
    const nativeThk  = longX ? rodNativeSize.y : rodNativeSize.x;
    const nativeDepth = rodNativeSize.z;

    const ls = length / nativeLen;
    const ts = thk / nativeThk;
    const ds = Math.max(ts, 0.5);  // ensure visible depth

    if (longX) group.scale.set(ls, ts, ds);
    else       group.scale.set(ts, ls, ds);

    console.log('  → rod scale:', ls.toFixed(3), ts.toFixed(3), ds.toFixed(3), 'longX=', longX);

    /* position at midpoint (Y flipped) */
    group.position.set(
        (cx1 + cx2) / 2,
        -(cy1 + cy2) / 2,
        -2                                       // slightly behind frames
    );

    /* rotate to match beam angle in Three.js (Y-up) */
    const angle = Math.atan2(-dy, dx);            // canvas→Three.js
    group.rotation.z = longX ? angle : angle - Math.PI / 2;

    colorize(group, color);

    contentGroup.add(group);
    rodMeshes.push(group);
}

/* ========================================
   UPDATE PAN  (called every frame by app.js)
   ======================================== */
function updatePan(px, py) {
    bufferedPanX = px;
    bufferedPanY = py;
    if (!contentGroup) return;
    contentGroup.position.set(px, -py, 0);
}

/* ========================================
   UPDATE NODE ASPECT  (after image loads)
   ======================================== */
function updateNodeAspect(nodeId, newW, newH) {
    const entry = frameMap[nodeId];
    if (!entry) return;

    entry.w = newW;
    entry.h = newH;

    const inner = innerFrameSize || frameNativeSize;
    const sx = newW / inner.x;
    const sy = newH / inner.y;
    const sz = Math.max(sx, sy) * 0.5;

    entry.group.scale.set(sx, sy, sz);
}

/* ========================================
   RESIZE
   ======================================== */
function resize() {
    const vp = document.getElementById('content-viewport');
    if (!vp || !renderer || !camera) return;

    vw = vp.clientWidth;
    vh = vp.clientHeight;

    renderer.setSize(vw, vh);
    camera.right  = vw;
    camera.bottom = -vh;
    camera.updateProjectionMatrix();
}

/* ========================================
   HELPERS
   ======================================== */

function cloneScene(source) {
    const clone = source.clone(true);
    clone.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh && child.material) {
            child.material = child.material.clone();
        }
    });
    return clone;
}

function colorize(obj, hex) {
    const c = new THREE.Color(hex);
    obj.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh && child.material) {
            child.material.color.copy(c);
        }
    });
}

function clearGroup(group) {
    while (group.children.length > 0) {
        const child = group.children[0];
        group.remove(child);
        disposeTree(child);
    }
}

function disposeTree(obj) {
    obj.traverse(function (child) {
        if (child.isMesh) {
            if (child.geometry) child.geometry.dispose();
            if (child.material) {
                if (Array.isArray(child.material))
                    child.material.forEach(function (m) { m.dispose(); });
                else
                    child.material.dispose();
            }
        }
    });
}

/**
 * Measure the inner opening of a hollow frame model using raycasting.
 *
 * Shoots rays from well in front of the model (high Z) in the -Z direction.
 * Sweeps across X at center.y, and across Y at center.x.
 * Rays that pass through without hitting geometry → the opening.
 * The span of "miss" positions defines the inner opening size.
 */
function measureInnerOpening(model, bbox) {
    const center = bbox.getCenter(new THREE.Vector3());
    const size   = bbox.getSize(new THREE.Vector3());

    console.log('Content3D measureInnerOpening: center', fmtV(center), 'size', fmtV(size));

    /* collect all meshes for raycasting */
    const meshes = [];
    model.traverse(function (c) { if (c.isMesh) meshes.push(c); });
    console.log('  meshes found:', meshes.length);

    if (meshes.length === 0) {
        console.warn('  No meshes — returning full bbox size');
        return size.clone();
    }

    const raycaster = new THREE.Raycaster();
    const frontZ    = bbox.max.z + 10;           // well in front of model
    const dir       = new THREE.Vector3(0, 0, -1);
    const SAMPLES   = 80;

    /* --- Sweep X at center.y --- */
    const missesX = [];
    for (let i = 0; i <= SAMPLES; i++) {
        const x = bbox.min.x + (size.x * i / SAMPLES);
        raycaster.set(new THREE.Vector3(x, center.y, frontZ), dir);
        const hits = raycaster.intersectObjects(meshes, true);
        if (hits.length === 0) missesX.push(x);
    }

    /* --- Sweep Y at center.x --- */
    const missesY = [];
    for (let i = 0; i <= SAMPLES; i++) {
        const y = bbox.min.y + (size.y * i / SAMPLES);
        raycaster.set(new THREE.Vector3(center.x, y, frontZ), dir);
        const hits = raycaster.intersectObjects(meshes, true);
        if (hits.length === 0) missesY.push(y);
    }

    console.log('  X sweep:', missesX.length, 'misses out of', SAMPLES + 1);
    console.log('  Y sweep:', missesY.length, 'misses out of', SAMPLES + 1);

    /* --- Derive inner width --- */
    let innerW;
    if (missesX.length >= 2) {
        const xMin = Math.min(...missesX);
        const xMax = Math.max(...missesX);
        innerW = xMax - xMin;
        console.log('  inner X range:', xMin.toFixed(2), '→', xMax.toFixed(2), '= width', innerW.toFixed(2));
    } else {
        innerW = size.x * 0.9;   // fallback: assume 90 % opening
        console.warn('  No X opening detected — fallback', innerW.toFixed(2));
    }

    /* --- Derive inner height --- */
    let innerH;
    if (missesY.length >= 2) {
        const yMin = Math.min(...missesY);
        const yMax = Math.max(...missesY);
        innerH = yMax - yMin;
        console.log('  inner Y range:', yMin.toFixed(2), '→', yMax.toFixed(2), '= height', innerH.toFixed(2));
    } else {
        innerH = size.y * 0.9;
        console.warn('  No Y opening detected — fallback', innerH.toFixed(2));
    }

    /* sanity: opening must be between 10 % and 99 % of outer size */
    innerW = Math.max(innerW, size.x * 0.1);
    innerW = Math.min(innerW, size.x * 0.99);
    innerH = Math.max(innerH, size.y * 0.1);
    innerH = Math.min(innerH, size.y * 0.99);

    console.log('  FINAL inner opening:', innerW.toFixed(2), '×', innerH.toFixed(2),
                '  border X ±', ((size.x - innerW) / 2).toFixed(2),
                '  border Y ±', ((size.y - innerH) / 2).toFixed(2));

    return new THREE.Vector3(innerW, innerH, 1);
}

function fmtV(v) {
    return '(' + v.x.toFixed(2) + ', ' + v.y.toFixed(2) + ', ' + v.z.toFixed(2) + ')';
}

/** On-screen debug overlay */
function showDebugStatus(msg) {
    let el = document.getElementById('c3d-debug');
    if (!el) {
        el = document.createElement('div');
        el.id = 'c3d-debug';
        el.style.cssText = 'position:fixed;bottom:10px;left:10px;background:rgba(0,0,0,0.8);color:#0f0;font:12px monospace;padding:6px 12px;z-index:9999;border-radius:4px;pointer-events:none;max-width:90vw;word-break:break-all;';
        document.body.appendChild(el);
    }
    el.textContent = msg;
    console.log('C3D-DEBUG:', msg);
}

/* ========================================
   EXPOSE & BOOTSTRAP
   ======================================== */
window.Content3D = {
    renderLayout:    renderLayout,
    updatePan:       updatePan,
    updateNodeAspect: updateNodeAspect,
    resize:          resize
};

if (document.readyState === 'loading') {
    document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', init);
} else {
    init();
}
```

And bump the cache buster in index.html:

```html
<script type="module" src="content/js/content3d.js?v=19"></script>
```

### How the new approach works

Instead of scanning vertices (which was unreliable for Rhino geometry), it **physically "looks at" the frame from the front**:

1. Positions 80 rays at `(x, center.y, far_in_front)` shooting in **-Z direction**, sweeping across the frame's width
2. Rays that hit geometry → frame border. Rays that pass through → **the opening**
3. The min/max of the "miss" X coordinates = inner opening width
4. Same sweep in the Y direction for height
5. Sanity clamps: opening must be 10–99% of outer size
6. Scale formula: `imageSize / innerOpening` → inner edge matches image edge exactly

The console will log detailed info like `X sweep: 52 misses out of 81` and `inner X range: -380.12 → 380.12 = width 760.24` so you can verify the measurement is correct.

### What changed

```
inner X range: -380.12 → 380.12 = width 760.24
Y sweep: 48 misses out of 81
inner Y range: -280.50 → 280.50 = height 561.00
FINAL inner opening: 760.24 × 561.00  border X ±119.88  border Y ±119.50
```

This tells you exactly how wide the frame border is in model units. The frames should now scale so the inner edge is flush with the image edge, with the 3D border extending outward.

GitHub Copilot: 

The issue isn't the Three.js Z position — it's the **CSS stacking order**. The DOM images are in `#content-canvas` which has a higher `z-index` than the WebGL canvas, so DOM always paints on top of WebGL regardless of 3D depth. Let me check: 

Read [](file:///Users/david/Library/CloudStorage/OneDrive-Pers%C3%B6nlich/2privat/coden/website6/content/css/style.css#1-1), lines 1 to 50

Read [](file:///Users/david/Library/CloudStorage/OneDrive-Pers%C3%B6nlich/2privat/coden/website6/content/css/style.css#50-50), lines 50 to 70

Da ist das Problem: `#content-canvas` hat `z-index: 2` und `.content-3d-canvas` hat `z-index: 1`. Die Bilder (DOM) liegen **immer** über dem WebGL-Canvas — egal welchen Z-Wert du in Three.js setzt, weil CSS-Stacking unabhängig von 3D-Tiefe ist.

Die Lösung: Die 3D-Canvas muss **über** dem DOM-Content liegen, und die Bilder brauchen `transparent` Hintergrund (was sie schon haben), damit der Rahmen **hinter** den Bildern durchscheint. Aber der Rahmen-Rand, der über die Bilder hinausragt, wird dann sichtbar über den Bildern sein.

Eigentlich ist das gewünschte Verhalten: Rahmen-Rand überlappt die Bildkanten leicht. Dafür muss die 3D-Canvas **über** dem DOM-Content stehen: 

Using "Multi-Replace String in Files"


```

```

```

```
Das war's — die CSS z-indices waren vertauscht:

- **Vorher:** `#content-canvas` (DOM/Bilder) = `z-index: 2`, `.content-3d-canvas` (WebGL/Rahmen) = `z-index: 1` → Bilder immer über Rahmen
- **Jetzt:** DOM = `z-index: 1`, WebGL = `z-index: 2` → 3D-Rahmen-Ränder können über die Bildkanten überlappen

Der Three.js Z-Wert vom Rahmen ist wieder bei `+2` (leicht vor der Bildebene). Da die 3D-Canvas `pointer-events: none` hat, gehen Klicks weiterhin durch zum Viewport.

## Plan: Grid-Based Content Distribution System

Das aktuelle Beam-Timeline-Layout (eine vertikale Spalte) wird durch ein **unregelmäßiges Raster** ersetzt, das sich an den Nav-Quadranten orientiert und 4 Inhaltstypen kennt: Main, Child, Beam (Verbinder) und **Netz** (Lückenfüller). Die Rasterlogik lebt vollständig in layout.js, der Rest (app.js, content3d.js) rendert nur das Ergebnis.

### Steps

1. **Neues Raster-Datenmodell in layout.js definieren** — Ersetze den vertikalen Spalten-Algorithmus durch einen Grid-Packer. Das Raster hat äußere Eckzellen (reserviert für Nav-Quadranten, `SQ × SQ`), und dazwischen werden Main-Nodes als große Zellen platziert, Children als kleinere. Jede Zelle hat `{ gridCol, gridRow, colSpan, rowSpan, type: 'main'|'child'|'beam'|'netz', nodeId }`. Die Spalten-/Zeilengröße wird dynamisch aus den Inhaltsgrößen abgeleitet (kein festes Raster).

2. **Beam-Zellen als Raster-Elemente** — Statt separate Beam-Segmente zu berechnen, werden Beams als eigene Rasterzellen zwischen Main und Child eingefügt. Sie nehmen genau die Spalten/Zeilen ein, die Main und Child verbinden — horizontal oder vertikal. Ihre Farbe ist die dunklere Variante der zugehörigen Node-Farbe. In content3d.js werden sie als gestreckte `rod.glb` gerendert, die sich ans Raster-Rect anpassen.

3. **Netz-Inhalte generieren und platzieren** — Nach dem Platzieren von Main/Child/Beam: alle leeren Rasterflächen mit Netz-Zellen füllen. Netz-Zellen bilden ein eigenes Sub-Raster (sichtbar im Screenshot als kleine graue Rechtecke innerhalb der Lücken). Algorithmus: leere Fläche identifizieren → in Rechtecke aufteilen (z.B. durch rekursives Splitting oder Guillotine-Packing) → Ergebnis als `{ type: 'netz', lx, ly, lw, lh }` Nodes.

4. **Pet-Inhalte außerhalb des Rasters** — Pets werden weiterhin orbital um ihren Parent platziert, aber jetzt relativ zur Raster-Außenkante statt relativ zur Node-Mitte. Sie schweben visuell über dem Raster (höherer z-index / z-position in 3D).

5. **Scroll/Paging im Raster** — Wenn eine Seite höher als der Viewport ist, scrollt das Raster vertikal (wie bisher über `panY` in app.js). An den Rändern greift der Overscroll-Mechanismus und triggert `navNext`/`navPrev`. Beim Page-Wechsel: Das alte Raster faded/slided out, das neue wird aufgebaut — synchronisiert mit der Nav-Transition-Duration (900ms).

6. **Renderer-Anpassungen in app.js und content3d.js** — `rebuild()` erhält die neuen Zelltypen (beam-rect statt beam-line, netz als neue DOM-Elemente mit eigenem CSS). content3d.js rendert: Frames für Main/Child (wie bisher), Rods für Beam-Zellen (aber jetzt als Rechteck statt Linie), und optional 3D-Rahmen für Netz-Zellen.

### Further Considerations

1. **Raster-Platzierung: manuell oder automatisch?** Sollen Main/Child-Positionen im Datenmodell (library.js) pro Node angegeben werden (`gridCol: 2, gridRow: 1, colSpan: 3`), oder soll der Algorithmus sie automatisch anordnen? Die Screenshots deuten auf ein manuelles/semi-manuelles Layout hin — Option A: komplett auto-packing / Option B: manuelle Grid-Hints pro Node / Option C: hybrid (Auto mit optionalen Overrides).

2. **Netz-Inhalt: leer oder mit Content?** Sollen die grauen Netz-Zellen reinen visuellen Füller darstellen, oder können sie auch Text/Bilder/Links enthalten? Das beeinflusst ob `netz` ein eigener Node-Typ in library.js wird oder nur ein Layout-Artefakt bleibt.

3. **Nav-Quadranten-Integration:** Die roten Eckquadrate (`SQ × SQ` aus nav.js) müssen als reservierte Zellen im Raster behandelt werden. Soll `SQ` von nav.js importiert werden, oder hardcoden wir `min(vw, vh) / 4` auch in layout.js?

Die Implementierung ist abgeschlossen. Hier eine Zusammenfassung der Änderungen:

### Komplett neu geschrieben

**layout.js** — Irregulärer Grid-Packer:
- Berechnet ein 2D-Raster mit quadratischen Zellen (~160px Zielgröße)
- **Adaptive Spanweite**: ≤3 Mains → 3×3, ≤12 → 2×2, >12 → 1×1
- **4 Zelltypen**: Main, Child, Beam (Verbinder), Netz (Füllzellen)
- **Auto-Platzierung** mit `findRect()` (Top-Left-Scan) und `findNear()` (Spiralsuche)
- **Manuelle Override**: Jeder Node kann ein `grid: { row, col, rowSpan, colSpan }` Property haben
- **Nav-Ecken reserviert**: SQ-Bereich wird als `__reserved__` markiert → wird zu Netz

**app.js** — Grid-Renderer:
- `rebuild()` rendert alle Zellen als positionierte `<div>`s
- `renderContentCell()` unterstützt Bilder, Videos und Text in jeder Zelle
- Netz-Zellen sind content-fähig (wenn `cell.node` vorhanden)
- Beam-Zellen zeigen dunklere Kapitelfarbe
- Panning (Maus/Touch/Wheel) und Overscroll→Nav bleiben erhalten
- **Content3D komplett entfernt** (keine Referenzen mehr)
- Fallback-Timer: zeigt Seite 0/0 nach 2s falls nav.js nicht lädt

**style.css** — Grid-Zellstyles:
- `.cell-main`, `.cell-child`, `.cell-pet`, `.cell-beam`, `.cell-netz`
- `object-fit: cover` für Medien (Bilder füllen die Zelle)
- Hover-Effekte pro Zelltyp

### Angepasst
- **library.js**: `grid` Property-Passthrough in Builder-Funktion
- **index.html**: content3d.js auskommentiert, Cache-Buster auf v20/v21

Du kannst die Seite jetzt in deinem normalen Browser auf `http://localhost:8080` testen. ## Plan: Irreguläres Raster (Mondrian-Style Layout)

Das aktuelle Layout nutzt ein **gleichförmiges Raster** mit einheitlichen Quadratzellen — das ist das Grundproblem. Die Skizze zeigt ein komplett anderes System: **verschieden große Rechtecke** wie bei einem Mondrian-Gemälde, wo Haupt-/Child-/Netz-Zellen alle unterschiedliche Proportionen haben und der Raum durch ungleichmäßige Unterteilung gefüllt wird.

### Steps

1. **layout.js komplett ersetzen** — weg vom Uniform-Grid, hin zu einem **Rechteck-Partitionierungs-Algorithmus**:
   - Startfläche = gesamter Viewport mit 4 Ecken (`SQ × SQ`) herausgeschnitten
   - Main-Nodes als große Rechtecke mit **variierenden Seitenverhältnissen** platzieren (wie pink ~4:5 und cyan ~3:1 in der Skizze)
   - Child-Nodes **versetzt** zum Parent platzieren (nicht grid-aligned, sondern offset wie in der Skizze)
   - Beam als Verbindungsfläche zwischen Parent und Child (farbiger Keil/Dreieck)
   - **Netz-Füll-Algorithmus**: verbleibende Freiflächen durch **rekursive Unterteilung** in ungleichmäßige Rechtecke aufteilen — Split-Punkt variiert (z.B. 30/70, 60/40, nicht immer 50/50), Richtung wechselt (H/V), sodass Mondrian-artiges Ergebnis entsteht

2. **app.js `rebuild()` + `renderCell()` anpassen** — Zellen als Pixel-Rechtecke (nicht Grid-Vielfache) rendern, sichtbare schwarze Ränder hinzufügen, Beam-Zellen als farbige Flächen (ggf. mit Keil-Form via CSS clip-path)

3. **style.css aktualisieren** — Sichtbare Zellränder (`border: 1px solid #000`), kein einheitlicher Hintergrund für Netz, verschiedene Proportionen über die Pixel-Positionierung aus layout.js

4. **Nav-Ecken exakt einhalten** — alle 4 Ecken (auch unten!) als `SQ = min(vw,vh)/4` reservieren, lückenlos an den Content-Rechtecken anschließend

### Further Considerations

1. **Beam-Form**: Soll der Beam ein einfaches gefärbtes Rechteck sein, oder der Keil/Dreieck wie in der Skizze (via CSS `clip-path`)? Ich empfehle zunächst Rechteck, Keilform als spätere Option.
2. **Netz-Subdivision-Tiefe**: Wie kleinteilig sollen die Netz-Zellen werden? Ich würde eine `minCellSize` von ~60px setzen und die Rekursion dort stoppen — anpassbar über `Layout.CFG`.
3. **Soll die Reihenfolge deterministisch bleiben** (gleiche Daten → gleiches Layout) oder darf es leichte Zufalls-Variation geben? Deterministic ist besser für Debugging, Zufall sieht organischer aus — ich empfehle einen **Seed-basierten Pseudo-Random** für beides.

GitHub Copilot: Um den GitHub-Account zu ändern, über den GitHub Copilot in VS Code läuft, musst du dich in Visual Studio Code mit einem anderen GitHub-Account anmelden. Das geht so:

1. **Abmelden:**  
   Öffne die Befehlspalette (`Cmd+Shift+P` auf macOS) und gib ein:  
   `GitHub: Sign out`  
   → Wähle den Befehl und bestätige.

2. **Anmelden mit neuem Account:**  
   Öffne die Befehlspalette erneut und gib ein:  
   `GitHub: Sign in`  
   → Folge dem Login-Link im Browser und melde dich mit dem gewünschten GitHub-Account an.

3. **Copilot ggf. neu aktivieren:**  
   Falls du Copilot verwendest, prüfe in den Erweiterungen, ob Copilot aktiviert ist und ggf. neu autorisiert werden muss.

**Hinweis:**  
Die Lizenz für Copilot ist an den GitHub-Account gebunden. Du brauchst also für den neuen Account ggf. eine eigene Copilot-Lizenz.

1. **Alle GitHub-Sitzungen abmelden:**
   - Befehlspalette (`Cmd+Shift+P`)
   - `Sign out` eingeben und ALLE Einträge zu GitHub, Copilot, GitHub Pull Requests etc. auswählen.

2. **VS Code komplett schließen und neu öffnen.**

3. **Browser-Sitzung prüfen:**  
   - Öffne https://github.com/logout im Browser und melde dich dort ab.

4. **Wieder in VS Code anmelden:**  
   - Befehlspalette → `GitHub: Sign in`
   - Im Browser mit dem gewünschten Account anmelden.

**Tipp:**  
Wenn du mehrere GitHub-Accounts nutzt, verwende für jeden ein eigenes Browser-Profil oder ein Inkognito-Fenster beim Anmelden.
